Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

آخر. المادة ١١ : من من النظام اللداخلي : تجري عمليات الانتخاب في المجلس بالاقتراع السري بواسطة طرف خاص واوراق تموذجية بيضاء يحمل
كلاهما ختم المجلس توزع على النواب وكل ظرف يتضمن اكثر من ورقة ؛ او يحمل علامة فارقة يعتبر
المادة 7١ من النظام الداخلي : لا تدخل في حساب الاغلبية. في اي انتشخاب يجريه المجلس, الاوراق البيضاء والملغاة
تعتبر ملغاة كل ورقة تتضمن :
- اسماء يفوق عددها. المراكز المحددة.
- او تحتوي على علامة تعريف او من اي نوع كانت. او تتضمن غير الاسم والشهرة مجردين. تتلف اوراق الانتخاب فور اعلان

===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:

0 وعلق رئيس الحكومة شفيق الوزان على الحادث بقوله
المتي جدا الاعتداء على النائب الدكتور حسن الرفاعي وانني استذكر اشد الاستتكار هذه الحادثة البشعة التي تزيد في آلامنا وتثقل على نفوسنا بعد سلسلة المآني التي توالت علينا
واضاف : ان جهودنا المبذولة لوقف ماساة لب
===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

الى الأرهاب

وقال نائب رئيس مجلس النواب مير ابو فاضل :؛ نستتكر اشمد الاستنكار الاعتداء الاثيم الذي تعرض له الزميل العزيز حسين الرفا ونطالب السلطات المحلية الى اتخلاما يمكن اتخاذه من اجزاءات صارمة لردع كل تعد على اي نائب لان للنائب حصانة مقدسة ولا سيما في هذا الظرف »
ريمون اده
© ودعا العميد ريمون اده النواب الى التعبير عن استذكارهم لحادث الاعتداء على زميلهم النائب حسن الرفاعي . بمقاطعة جلسة مجلس النواب التي دعا لعقدها الرئيس كامل الاسعد اليوم في احدى الثكنات العسكرية ١ .
وقال اده في اتصال هاتفي من باريس : , ان الواجب يحتم على كل نائب يحترم نفسه ان يحدد موققا واضحاً يكف التهديدات والضغوط التي تمارس_من اجهات بات الجميع يعرفها , للوصول الى نتيجة معينة في انتخاب رئيس الجمهورية . .
وقال مستطردا : ,ان وقوف الذواب مثل هذا الموقف لا يعني الانتصار لكراماتهم فحسب . بل يعني الانتصار للحرية والديموقراطية اللتين بدونهما يفقد لبنان الكثير من اخصائص وجوده ٠
Answer: Structure: Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness
Explanation: The text is describing the president in a lot of details. The text is also using words such as "the president", which shows that it is describing the president in a lot of details.

وان هذا الاعتداء ان دل على شيء قائما ‏ يدل على همجية ويد مجرمة تطال رجل القانون والراي الحر ء والصلب من اجل الحقيقة والميادىء الديتقراطية في هذا الظرف الدقيق الذي يمر به لبنان ٠
واضاف حمادة : ١ ان هذه الجريمة التي تعرض لها التائب الرفاعي عمل منكر ينبىء بما يعد لنا في ظل لبئان الجديد 6
ورحب الوزير مروان حمادة باللقاء الذي تم بين الرئيس كميل شمعون ووليد جتبلاط قائلا: ‏ ان _مثل هذه اللقاءات من شانها انقاذ لبنان ووحدته ونظامه الديمقراطي ».

اضاف: ؛ واننا في كتلة تواب بعليك الهرمل.إذ نستذكر الجريمة اشد الاستتكار فاتنا نتعهد بعدم التهاون في ملاحقتها وكشف حقيقتها ٠
Answer: Sentence: ان هذه الجريمة التي تعرض لها التائب الرفاعي عمل منكر ينبىء
===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

ٌ
دبلوماسي من الامارات
الكويت -؟؟ ٠ فاب - قال مسؤولون كو تيون ان دبلوماسيا كبيرا من دولة الامارات تعرض لمحاولة اغتيال اليوم حين اطلق عليه اردني ١ ادعى انه صحاق ؛ النار في مكتيه فجرحة .

وذكرت الشرطة انه تم اعتقال مطلق النار الذي يحمل جواز سفر اردنيا ويجري استجوابه . لكنها لم تذكر دوافعة او اسمه

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>

If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Text: التيار الكهربائي اعيد وقطع مرات عدة [ص؟] النساء ينهين اعتصامهن قي الاميركية [ص؛ ]
الاميركية - الصهيوتنية - الرجعية الرامية الى تصفية القضيةالفلسطينية وتمرير الحلقات التالية من مخططات كامب ديفيد . يعمل النظام العراقي جاهداً على تطوير هتعرّيز علاقاته مع النظام المصري لتصل الى درجة التحالف المعلن من خلال حوار اتسم في البداية بشيء من السرية ثم اخذ طابعه الاعلاني حيال موقف الصمت والتخاذل العربي ٠ . واضاف ,واستشماراً هنا بالمسؤولية القومية والتاريخية وحرصنا المستمر على وجوب تاكيد اهمية الاحترام والتقيد بقرار الجبهة القومية للصمود والتصدي في مقاومة كل انحراف يظهر في القضية العربية . ارى من مسؤوليتي ان انيه الى المخاطر المترتبة على السكوت حيال التحالف المصري - العراقي والمتمثلة فيما ياتي - ان التحائف المعلن بين الحكومة العراقية والنظام المصري بعد علاقة رسمعية مع الخيانة . وانتهاكاً صارخاً لقرارات قمة بقداد التي ارست قاعدة الحد الادنى في العمل العربي المشترك ووضعت النظام المصري على القائمة السوداء - ان التحالف بين نظامي بغداد
:أ والقاهرة يشكل سابقة جديدة تضاف الى
سايقات اخرى وان عدم التصدي لها قد يمهد الطريق لانظمة عربية اخرى تعمل الآن من أجل الالتقاف على قرارات قمة بغداد واسقاطها
ان الصمت العربي حيال التحالف والاتصالات العلنية المستمرة بين الحكومة العراقية والنظام المصري يعني امكانية التتصل من اي قرار او ميثاق عربي دونما عقاب او أدانة كما يعني في الوقت ذاته الاقرار بعدم جدوى وجدبة أي فعل او اجتماع عربي حتى وان كان على مستوى القمة
- ان النظام العراقي بانحرافه عن الاجماع العربي . قد اسهم في تقويض ركن من اساسيات العمل القومي المشترك المرتكز على رفض ومقاومة مخططات كامب ديفيد ويصح اعتباره
ومضى بقول ؛ واقتناعاً منا بخطورة المنزلق الجديد الذي تردى فيه النظام العراقي وما يمكن ان يرتبه من مضاعفات سلبية على المسيرة النضالية للامة العربية . قاننا نعتقد باهمية قيام اقطار الجبهة القومية للصمود والتصدي بتحرك منسق وفعال لكشف وتعرية هذا التحالف التتمة ص 8 )

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

وقد عقد اجتماع في قصر بعبدا امس بين الرئيس الياس سركيس والرئيس شفيق الوزان ووزير الخارجية فؤاد بطرس من جهة
===================================================

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

Bachir Gemayel was the commander of Lebanese forces, which was the military wing of the Kataeb party during the Lebanese Civil War.
The Palestinian presence through the PLO as well as the Syrian presence was angering many Lebanese leftists, and the IDF had plans of rooting up the PLO threat to Israel.
Gemayel allied with Israel and his forces fought the PLO and the Syrian Army.
The context above generated a lot of controversy with differing stances towards Gemayel and the Ktaeb Party, which was demonstrated through many Lebanese newspapers.
You will be given excerpts of text from Lebanese newspapers, and your task is to identify the presence of text structures and strategies that talk about the topic above using either of the following ways:
* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group

If any of the above structures is found in the text, output the: (1) sentence(s) and (2) the corresponding structure(s) name(s), (3) the explanation in the following format:
Sentence: <the sentence>, Structure(s): <teh structure(s)>, Explanation: <the explanation>
Out each extracted sentence, and its corresponding structure(s) and explanation on a separate line.
If none of the structures if found, output "None".

* Extreme levels of description and degrees of completeness: Sentence describing a certain group with a lot of details or with some vagueness
* Implications: Sentence that uses certain pronouns that imply negative things about a certain group.
* Denominations: Sentence that describes one group as being different from another group that especially uses words such as immigrants, others, opponents, and so on.
* Agency: Sentence that holds a certain group responsible for certain negative actions with emphasis on their agency
* Focus: Sentence that focuses on certain textual aspects such as participants or actions
* Demonstratives: Sentence that signals closeness or distance to a certain group.
* Pronouns: Sentence that uses words such as 'us' and 'them' to classify in-groups or out-groups
* Active/Passive Sentences: Active sentence associated with negative actions of a group, or passive sentences associated with positive actions of a group
